## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Solid Mechanics
**Analysis**: The variables correspond to stress, strain, and temperature, which are core parameters in constitutive modeling and thermomechanics. The relationship likely describes how a material's mechanical response evolves with deformation and thermal conditions, involving concepts like Hooke's law, thermal expansion, strain hardening, and thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Thermoelastic linear model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (Hooke's law accounting for thermal strain offset)
- Temperature-modulated elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear stiffness varying with temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood nonlinear plasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (smooth transition from elastic to plastic regime)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening degraded by temperature)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (stress approaching asymptotic flow limit due to dislocation saturation)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * T**2 (bilinear and quadratic thermal stress contributions)
- Hyperbolic tangent plasticity: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) + c2 * T (bounded stress response with linear thermal shift)
- Linear thermal degradation: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Exponential thermal degradation: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * epsilon (rapid modulus loss at high temperatures)
- Phase-transition modulated stiffness: sigma = c0 * (1 + tanh(c1 * (T - c2))) * epsilon (sigmoidal change in modulus near phase transformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mechanical vs thermal strain partitioning → Difference structure (epsilon - c*T) inside a modulus function
- Strain hardening behavior → Monotonically increasing nonlinearity like epsilon**c (c>1) or epsilon + c*epsilon**2 reflecting dislocation accumulation
- Thermal softening/stiffening → Multiplicative temperature scaling (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c*T) on strain terms, distinct from generic decay/growth
- Asymptotic plastic flow → Saturated exponential (1 - exp(c*epsilon)) or tanh for dislocation density limits
- Thermo-mechanical work coupling → Cross terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c*T representing temperature-dependent hardening rates
- Elastic-plastic knee transition → Smooth polynomial blend c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 capturing the yield point without sharp discontinuities
- Phase transformation effects → Sigmoidal temperature dependence tanh(c*(T-c)) modulating stiffness or yield strength

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon*c4*(T - c5)**c6`
GT numerical expression: `21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*(T - 342.5784399345082) + 1) + epsilon*5.6497230214391285*(T - 342.5784399345082)**2`
Let's simplify the GT expression algebraically.
Let $E = \epsilon$, $T = T$.
GT = $c_0 E (-c_1 (T - c_2) + c_3) + E c_4 (T - c_5)^{c_6}$
From numerical values:
$c_0 \approx 21.698$
$c_1 \approx 0.0546$
$c_2 \approx 342.578$
$c_3 = 1$
$c_4 \approx 5.6497$
$c_5 \approx 342.578$ (same as $c_2$)
$c_6 = 2$

So GT = $c_0 E (-c_1 T + c_1 c_2 + c_3) + c_4 E (T - c_2)^2$
GT = $E [ c_0 (-c_1 T + c_1 c_2 + c_3) + c_4 (T^2 - 2 c_2 T + c_2^2) ]$
GT = $E [ c_4 T^2 + (-c_0 c_1 - 2 c_4 c_2) T + (c_0 c_1 c_2 + c_0 c_3 + c_4 c_2^2) ]$
This is a polynomial in $T$ of degree 2, multiplied by $\epsilon$.
Specifically, GT = $\epsilon (A T^2 + B T + C)$, where $A, B, C$ are constants.
Let's check the structure: $\epsilon \times (\text{quadratic in } T)$.
So GT is of the form $\epsilon (c_a T^2 + c_b T + c_c)$.

Let's verify this structure.
GT = $c_0 \epsilon (-c_1 T + c_1 c_2 + c_3) + c_4 \epsilon (T - c_2)^2$
$= \epsilon [ -c_0 c_1 T + c_0(c_1 c_2 + c_3) + c_4(T^2 - 2c_2 T + c_2^2) ]$
$= \epsilon [ c_4 T^2 + (-c_0 c_1 - 2 c_4 c_2) T + (c_0 c_1 c_2 + c_0 c_3 + c_4 c_2^2) ]$
Yes, it's exactly $\epsilon (A T^2 + B T + C)$.

Let's quickly verify Candidate 22 again just in case.
`epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*(T + c5)**2*(c6 + epsilon))/(c6 + epsilon)`
$= \epsilon \left( \frac{T c_0 \epsilon + T c_1 + c_2 \epsilon + c_3}{c_6 + \epsilon} + c_4 (T+c_5)^2 \right)$
For this to equal $\epsilon (A T^2 + B T + C)$, the fraction must be constant w.r.t $\epsilon$.
$\frac{T c_0 \epsilon + T c_1 + c_2 \epsilon + c_3}{c_6 + \epsilon} = K(T)$.
This requires numerator to be $K(T)(c_6 + \epsilon)$.
So $T c_0 \epsilon + T c_1 + c_2 \epsilon + c_3 = K(T) c_6 + K(T) \epsilon$.
Comparing coefficients of $\epsilon$: $T c_0 + c_2 = K(T)$.
Comparing constant terms: $T c_1 + c_3 = K(T) c_6$.
So $K(T) = c_0 T + c_2$.
Then $T c_1 + c_3 = (c_0 T + c_2) c_6 = c_0 c_6 T + c_2 c_6$.
This implies $c_1 = c_0 c_6$ and $c_3 = c_2 c_6$.
If we set $c_1 = c_0 c_6$ and $c_3 = c_2 c_6$, then the fraction becomes exactly $c_0 T + c_2$.
Then Candidate 22 becomes $\epsilon (c_0 T + c_2 + c_4 (T+c_5)^2)$.
This is $\epsilon (c_4 T^2 + (c_0 + 2 c_4 c_5) T + (c_2 + c_4 c_5^2))$.
This matches the form $\epsilon (A T^2 + B T + C)$!
Wait, I missed this algebraic simplification for Candidate 22.
Let's verify:
If $c_1 = c_0 c_6$ and $c_3 = c_2 c_6$, then:
Numerator: $T c_0 \epsilon + T c_0 c_6 + c_2 \epsilon + c_2 c_6 = c_0 T (\epsilon + c_6) + c_2 (\epsilon + c_6) = (c_0 T + c_2)(\epsilon + c_6)$.
Divided by $(\epsilon + c_6)$, it gives $c_0 T + c_2$.
So Candidate 22 simplifies to $\epsilon (c_0 T + c_2 + c_4 (T+c_5)^2)$.
This is exactly a quadratic in $T$ multiplied by $\epsilon$.
So Candidate 22 is ALSO a MATCH!

If $c_2=0$, numerator is $T c_0 \epsilon + T c_1 + c_4 \epsilon + c_5 = \epsilon(T c_0 + c_4) + (T c_1 + c_5)$.
We want this to be $(c_3 + \epsilon) K(T) = c_3 K(T) + \epsilon K(T)$.

And $c_3 K(T) = T c_1 + c_5 \Rightarrow c_3(T c_0 + c_4) = T c_1 + c_5$.
This implies $c_1 = c_3 c_0$ and $c_5 = c_3 c_4$.
If we set $c_2=0, c_1=c_3 c_0, c_5=c_3 c_4$, then Candidate 1 becomes $\epsilon K(T) = \epsilon (c_0 T + c_4)$.
This is linear in $T$, not quadratic. GT is quadratic. So Candidate 1 cannot match GT.

### Analysis of Ground Truth
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon*c4*(T - c5)**c6`
Given the numerical value `c6 = 2.0`, the term `(T - c5)**c6` is a quadratic polynomial in `T`. Expanding the GT yields:
`GT = epsilon * [ c4*T**2 + (-c0*c1 - 2*c4*c5)*T + (c0*c1*c2 + c0*c3 + c4*c5**2) ]`
Thus, the GT is structurally equivalent to **`epsilon * (A*T**2 + B*T + C)`**, where `A, B, C` are constant coefficients independent of `epsilon` and `T`. Any candidate that can be algebraically reduced to this exact form (by freely assigning values to its constants) is a match. Candidates containing `sqrt(T)`, `exp(T)`, `sin(T)`, `log(T)`, `1/T`, or rational functions of `epsilon` that cannot cancel out are rejected.

### Candidate Evaluation
- **Candidate 1:** Rational function in `epsilon` with an `epsilon**2` term in the numerator. Cannot reduce to a polynomial in `T`. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 2:** `epsilon*(c0*epsilon**2 + c1 + c2*epsilon + c3*(T + c4)**2)`. Setting `c0=0` and `c2=0` yields `epsilon*(c1 + c3*(T+c4)**2)`, which expands to `epsilon*(c3*T**2 + 2*c3*c4*T + c1 + c3*c4**2)`. Matches the GT structure. `[MATCH]`

- **Candidate 22:** `epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*(T + c5)**2*(c6 + epsilon))/(c6 + epsilon)`. By setting `c1 = c0*c6` and `c3 = c2*c6`, the fraction simplifies: `(T*c0*(epsilon+c6) + c2*(epsilon+c6))/(c6+epsilon) = c0*T + c2`. ## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*(T - 342.5784399345082) + 1) + epsilon*5.6497230214391285*(T - 342.5784399345082)**2
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `21.698...*epsilon*(-0.0546...*(T - 342.578...) + 1)`
  = `21.698...*epsilon*(-0.0546...*T + 0.0546...*342.578... + 1)`
  = `21.698...*epsilon*(-0.0546...*T + 18.707... + 1)`
  = `21.698...*epsilon*(-0.0546...*T + 19.707...)`
  = `-1.1848...*epsilon*T + 427.63...*epsilon`

Wait, let me recalculate more carefully.

c0*c1 = 21.698... * 0.05460... = 1.18488...
c0*c1*c2 = 1.18488... * 342.578... = 405.93...
c0*c3 = 21.698... * 1 = 21.698...

First term expanded: `epsilon*(-c0*c1*T + c0*c1*c2 + c0*c3)` = `epsilon*(-1.18488*T + 405.93 + 21.698)` = `epsilon*(-1.18488*T + 427.63)`

Second term: `epsilon*5.6497*(T - 342.578)^2` = `epsilon*5.6497*(T^2 - 685.157*T + 117,360)` = `5.6497*epsilon*T^2 - 3871.0*epsilon*T + 662,975*epsilon`

So GT = `epsilon*(-1.18488*T + 427.63) + epsilon*(5.6497*T^2 - 3871.0*T + 662,975)`
= `5.6497*epsilon*T^2 + epsilon*(-1.18488 - 3871.0)*T + epsilon*(427.63 + 662,975)`
= `5.6497*epsilon*T^2 - 3872.18*epsilon*T + 663,403*epsilon`

So GT is: **epsilon * (A*T^2 + B*T + C)** where A, B, C are specific constants.

This can also be written as: `epsilon*(c_a*(T + c_b)^2 + c_c*T + c_d)` or simply `epsilon*(a*T^2 + b*T + c)`.

The key structural requirement: GT = epsilon × (quadratic in T). No other variables, no sqrt(T), no sin, no exp, no epsilon^2, etc.

### Candidate 1:
`epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon*(c3 + epsilon) + c4*epsilon + c5)/(c3 + epsilon)`

This has epsilon-dependent rational structure. Let me expand numerator:
`epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon*c3 + T*c2*epsilon^2 + c4*epsilon + c5)`

Dividing by (c3 + epsilon): This gives a rational function in epsilon, not a polynomial. GT is `epsilon*(aT^2 + bT + c)` which is polynomial in both epsilon and T. This can't match unless the division simplifies perfectly.

For it to equal `epsilon*(aT^2 + bT + c)`, we need:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon*(c3+epsilon) + c4*epsilon + c5 = (aT^2+bT+c)*(c3+epsilon)`

RHS = `aT^2*c3 + aT^2*epsilon + bT*c3 + bT*epsilon + c*c3 + c*epsilon`

LHS = `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*c3*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon^2 + c4*epsilon + c5`

Comparing T^2 terms: RHS has `aT^2*c3 + aT^2*epsilon`, LHS has none. So a=0, but GT requires a≠0. 

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 22:
`epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*(T + c5)**2*(c6 + epsilon))/(c6 + epsilon)`

Let me expand. Numerator:
`epsilon*(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*(T+c5)^2*c6 + c4*(T+c5)^2*epsilon)`

For this to equal `epsilon*(aT^2+bT+c)*(c6+epsilon)/(c6+epsilon)` = `epsilon*(aT^2+bT+c)`:

We need: `(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*(T+c5)^2*(c6+epsilon))/(c6+epsilon) = aT^2+bT+c`

Let me denote D = c6+epsilon. Then:
`(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3)/D + c4*(T+c5)^2`

For the first part to be independent of epsilon (since GT is), we need:
`(T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3)/(c6+epsilon)`

= `((T*c0+c2)*epsilon + T*c1+c3)/(c6+epsilon)`

For this to be independent of epsilon, we need: `(T*c0+c2)*epsilon + T*c1+c3 = K*(c6+epsilon)` for some K.

This means: T*c0+c2 = K and T*c1+c3 = K*c6.

From first: K = T*c0+c2
From second: T*c1+c3 = (T*c0+c2)*c6 = T*c0*c6 + c2*c6

So: T*c1+c3 = T*c0*c6 + c2*c6
→ c1 = c0*c6 and c3 = c2*c6

Then K = T*c0+c2, and the expression becomes:
`T*c0+c2 + c4*(T+c5)^2`

So the full expression is: `epsilon*(T*c0 + c2 + c4*(T+c5)^2)`
= `epsilon*(c4*T^2 + (2*c4*c5+c0)*T + c4*c5^2+c2)`

This is `epsilon*(quadratic in T)`. ✓ This matches the GT structure!

We need: c4 = 5.6497, 2*c4*c5+c0 = -3872.18, c4*c5^2+c2 = 663,403.

With c5 = -342.578: 2*5.6497*(-342.578) + c0 = -3872.18 → -3870.99 + c0 = -3872.18 → c0 = -1.185 ✓
c4*c5^2+c2 = 5.6497*117,360 + c2 = 663,003 + c2 = 663,403 → c2 ≈ 400 ✓

And constraints c1 = c0*c6, c3 = c2*c6 are satisfiable with free constants.

Candidate 22 verdict: [MATCH]
